				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Nike_(company)&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Nike (company)">Nike (company)</a>)</span></div>
			</div>
			
			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the sportswear and apparel company. For other uses of the name "Nike", see <a href="/wiki/Nike_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Nike (disambiguation)">Nike (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Nike, Inc.</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/aɪ/: 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>)<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[note 1]</a></sup> is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a> that is engaged in the design, development, manufacturing, and worldwide marketing and sales of footwear, apparel, equipment, accessories, and services. The company is headquartered near <a href="/wiki/Beaverton,_Oregon" title="Beaverton, Oregon">Beaverton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Portland_metropolitan_area" title="Portland metropolitan area">Portland metropolitan area</a>. It is the world's largest supplier of <a href="/wiki/Sneakers" title="Sneakers">athletic shoes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clothing" title="Clothing">apparel</a><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[3]</a></sup> and a major manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Sports_equipment" title="Sports equipment">sports equipment</a>, with revenue in excess of US$24.1 billion in its fiscal year 2012 (ending May 31, 2012). As of 2012, it employed more than 44,000 people worldwide. In 2014 the brand alone was valued at $19 billion, making it the most valuable brand among sports businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[4]</a></sup> As of 2017, the Nike brand is valued at $29.6 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[5]</a></sup> Nike ranked No. 89 in the 2018 <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[6]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://nike.com">nike<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;line-height: 1.35em;"><b>Footnotes / references</b><br><sup id="cite_ref-10K2017_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10K2017-1">[1]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:15-08-NikeFactoryStore_Wisconsin_IMG_1218.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/15-08-NikeFactoryStore_Wisconsin_IMG_1218.JPG/220px-15-08-NikeFactoryStore_Wisconsin_IMG_1218.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592"></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:15-08-NikeFactoryStore_Wisconsin_IMG_1218.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nike Factory Store in Wisconsin</div></div></div>
<p>The company was founded on January 25, 1964, as <b>Blue Ribbon Sports</b>, by <a href="/wiki/Bill_Bowerman" title="Bill Bowerman">Bill Bowerman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phil_Knight" title="Phil Knight">Phil Knight</a>, and officially became Nike, Inc. on May 30, 1971. The company takes its name from <a href="/wiki/Nike_(mythology)" title="Nike (mythology)">Nike</a>, the Greek goddess of victory.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[7]</a></sup> Nike markets its products under its own brand, as well as Nike Golf, Nike Pro, <a href="/wiki/Nike%2B" title="Nike+">Nike+</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Jordan" title="Air Jordan">Air Jordan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nike_Blazers" title="Nike Blazers">Nike Blazers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Force_1_(shoe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Force 1 (shoe)">Air Force 1</a>, Nike Dunk, <a href="/wiki/Air_Max" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Max">Air Max</a>, Foamposite, <a href="/wiki/Nike_Skateboarding" title="Nike Skateboarding">Nike Skateboarding</a>, Nike CR7,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> and subsidiaries including Brand Jordan,  and <a href="/wiki/Converse_(shoe_company)" title="Converse (shoe company)">Converse</a>. Nike also owned Bauer Hockey (later renamed <a href="/wiki/Bauer_Hockey" title="Bauer Hockey">Nike Bauer</a>) from 1995 to 2008, and previously owned <a href="/wiki/Cole_Haan" title="Cole Haan">Cole Haan</a> <a href="/wiki/Umbro" title="Umbro">Umbro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hurley_International" title="Hurley International">Hurley International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> In addition to manufacturing sportswear and equipment, the company operates retail stores under the Niketown name. Nike sponsors many high-profile athletes and sports teams around the world, with the highly recognized trademarks of "<a href="/wiki/Just_Do_It" title="Just Do It">Just Do It</a>" and the <a href="/wiki/Swoosh" title="Swoosh">Swoosh</a> logo.
</p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins_and_history">Origins and history</span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Nike_logo.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Old_Nike_logo.jpg/220px-Old_Nike_logo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="375" data-file-height="197"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 116px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Old_Nike_logo.jpg/220px-Old_Nike_logo.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="116" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Nike_logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Old logo of Nike, Inc., still used on some retro products with red boxes</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NikeFactoryStoreVaughanMills.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/NikeFactoryStoreVaughanMills.JPG/220px-NikeFactoryStoreVaughanMills.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="332" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4928"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 332px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/NikeFactoryStoreVaughanMills.JPG/220px-NikeFactoryStoreVaughanMills.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="332" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NikeFactoryStoreVaughanMills.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Nike Factory Store in <a href="/wiki/Vaughan_Mills" title="Vaughan Mills">Vaughan Mills</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nike_Harajuku_interior_2018.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Nike_Harajuku_interior_2018.jpg/220px-Nike_Harajuku_interior_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="1824"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Nike_Harajuku_interior_2018.jpg/220px-Nike_Harajuku_interior_2018.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nike_Harajuku_interior_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Nike Store in <a href="/wiki/Harajuku" title="Harajuku">Harajuku</a>, Tokyo, Japan</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nike_Kicks_Lounge_in_Harbour_City_2017.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Nike_Kicks_Lounge_in_Harbour_City_2017.jpg/220px-Nike_Kicks_Lounge_in_Harbour_City_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="1408"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 147px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Nike_Kicks_Lounge_in_Harbour_City_2017.jpg/220px-Nike_Kicks_Lounge_in_Harbour_City_2017.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="147" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nike_Kicks_Lounge_in_Harbour_City_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nike Kicks Lounge in <a href="/wiki/Harbour_City_(Hong_Kong)" title="Harbour City (Hong Kong)">Harbour City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a></div></div></div>
<p>Nike, originally known as Blue Ribbon Sports (BRS), was founded by <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oregon" title="University of Oregon">University of Oregon</a> track athlete <a href="/wiki/Phil_Knight" title="Phil Knight">Phil Knight</a> and his coach, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Bowerman" title="Bill Bowerman">Bill Bowerman</a>, on January 25, 1964.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> The company initially operated in <a href="/wiki/Eugene,_Oregon" title="Eugene, Oregon">Eugene</a>, Oregon as a distributor for Japanese shoe maker <a href="/wiki/Onitsuka_Tiger" title="Onitsuka Tiger">Onitsuka Tiger</a>, making most sales at track meets out of Knight's automobile.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup></p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Otis_Davis" title="Otis Davis">Otis Davis</a>, a University of Oregon student athlete coached by Bowerman and Olympic gold medalist at the <a href="/wiki/1960_Summer_Olympics" title="1960 Summer Olympics">1960 Summer Olympics</a>, his coach made the first pair of Nike shoes for him, contradicting a claim that they were made for Phil Knight. According to Davis, "I told <a href="/wiki/Tom_Brokaw" title="Tom Brokaw">Tom Brokaw</a> that I was the first. I don't care what all the billionaires say. Bill Bowerman made the first pair of shoes for me. People don't believe me. In fact, I didn't like the way they felt on my feet. There was no support and they were too tight. But I saw Bowerman made them from the <a href="/wiki/Waffle_iron" title="Waffle iron">waffle iron</a>, and they were mine".<sup id="cite_ref-HudReporter2006_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HudReporter2006-13">[12]</a></sup></p><p>In its first year in business, BRS sold 1,300 pairs of Japanese running shoes grossing $8,000.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> By 1965, sales had reached $20,000. In 1966, BRS opened its first retail store at 3107 Pico Boulevard in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Monica,_California" title="Santa Monica, California">Santa Monica, California</a>. In 1967, due to increasing sales, BRS expanded retail and distribution operations on the East Coast, in <a href="/wiki/Wellesley,_Massachusetts" title="Wellesley, Massachusetts">Wellesley, Massachusetts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup></p><p>By 1971, the relationship between BRS and Onitsuka Tiger came to an end. BRS prepared to launch its own line of footwear, which was rebranded as Nike, and would bear the <a href="/wiki/Swoosh" title="Swoosh">Swoosh</a> newly designed by <a href="/wiki/Carolyn_Davidson" title="Carolyn Davidson">Carolyn Davidson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> The Swoosh was first used by Nike on June 18, 1971, and was registered with the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Patent_and_Trademark_Office" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Patent and Trademark Office">U.S. Patent and Trademark Office</a> on January 22, 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="This claim needs references to better sources. (January 2020)">better source needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 1976, the company hired John Brown and Partners, based in Seattle, as its first advertising agency.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-18">[17]</a></sup> The following year, the agency created the first "brand ad" for Nike, called "There is no finish line", in which no Nike product was shown.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-18">[17]</a></sup> By 1980, Nike had attained a 50% market share in the U.S. athletic shoe market, and the company went public in December of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup></p><p><a href="/wiki/Wieden%2BKennedy" title="Wieden+Kennedy">Wieden+Kennedy</a>, Nike's primary ad agency, has worked with Nike to create many print and television advertisements, and Wieden+Kennedy remains Nike's primary ad agency.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It was agency co-founder <a href="/wiki/Dan_Wieden" title="Dan Wieden">Dan Wieden</a> who coined the now-famous slogan "<a href="/wiki/Just_Do_It" title="Just Do It">Just Do It</a>" for a 1988 Nike ad campaign,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> which was chosen by <i>Advertising Age</i> as one of the top five ad slogans of the 20th century and enshrined in the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian Institution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Walt_Stack" title="Walt Stack">Walt Stack</a> was featured in Nike's first "Just Do It" advertisement, which debuted on July 1, 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> Wieden credits the inspiration for the slogan to "Let's do it", the last words spoken by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Gilmore_(criminal)" title="Gary Gilmore (criminal)">Gary Gilmore</a> before he was executed.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-23">[22]</a></sup></p><p>Throughout the 1980s, Nike expanded its product line to encompass many sports and regions throughout the world.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> In 1990, Nike moved into its eight-building World Headquarters campus in Beaverton, Oregon.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> The first Nike retail store, dubbed Niketown, opened in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Portland" class="mw-redirect" title="Downtown Portland">downtown Portland</a> in November of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-Niketown_to_close_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Niketown_to_close-26">[25]</a></sup></p><p>Phil Knight announced in mid-2015 that he would step down as chairman of Nike in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> He officially stepped down from all duties with the company on June 30, 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup></p><p>In a company public announcement on March 15, 2018, Nike CEO <a href="/wiki/Mark_Parker" title="Mark Parker">Mark Parker</a> said Trevor Edwards, a top Nike executive who was seen as a potential successor to the chief executive, was relinquishing his position as Nike's brand president and would retire in August.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2019, <a href="/wiki/John_Donahoe" title="John Donahoe">John Donahoe</a> was announced as the next CEO, and succeeded Parker on January 13, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_LP_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_LP-31">[30]</a></sup> In November 2019, the company stopped selling directly through <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a>, focusing more on direct relationships with customers.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions">Acquisitions</span></h3>
<p>Nike has acquired and sold several apparel and footwear companies over the course of its history. Its first acquisition was the upscale footwear company <a href="/wiki/Cole_Haan" title="Cole Haan">Cole Haan</a> in 1988,<sup id="cite_ref-colehaanacquired_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colehaanacquired-33">[32]</a></sup> followed by the purchase of <a href="/wiki/Bauer_Hockey" title="Bauer Hockey">Bauer Hockey</a> in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-bauerdivestment_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauerdivestment-34">[33]</a></sup> In 2002, Nike bought surf apparel company <a href="/wiki/Hurley_International" title="Hurley International">Hurley International</a> from founder <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hurley" title="Bob Hurley">Bob Hurley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hurleyacquired_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hurleyacquired-35">[34]</a></sup> In 2003, Nike paid US$309 million to acquire sneaker company <a href="/wiki/Converse_(shoe_company)" title="Converse (shoe company)">Converse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup> The company acquired <a href="/wiki/Starter_Clothing_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Starter Clothing Line">Starter</a> in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-starteracq_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-starteracq-37">[36]</a></sup> and soccer uniform maker <a href="/wiki/Umbro" title="Umbro">Umbro</a> in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-umbroacqanddivest_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umbroacqanddivest-38">[37]</a></sup></p><p>In order to refocus its business lines, Nike began divesting of some of its subsidiaries in the 2000s.<sup id="cite_ref-chaan_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chaan-39">[38]</a></sup> It sold Starter in 2007<sup id="cite_ref-starteracq_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-starteracq-37">[36]</a></sup> and Bauer Hockey in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-bauerdivestment_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bauerdivestment-34">[33]</a></sup> The company sold Umbro in 2012 <sup id="cite_ref-umbrodivestment_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-umbrodivestment-40">[39]</a></sup> and Cole Haan in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-colehaandivestment_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-colehaandivestment-41">[40]</a></sup> As of 2020, Nike owns only one subsidiary: <a href="/wiki/Converse_(shoe_company)" title="Converse (shoe company)">Converse Inc.</a>
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span></h3>
<p>Nike bought back $8 billion of Nike's class B stock in four years after the current $5 billion buyback program was completed in the second quarter of fiscal year 2013. Up to September 2012, Nike Inc. has bought back $10 billion of stock.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup></p><p>Nike was made a member of the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a> in 2013, when it replaced <a href="/wiki/Alcoa" title="Alcoa">Alcoa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Barron's_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barron's-43">[42]</a></sup></p><p>On December 19, 2013, Nike's quarterly profit rose due to a 13 percent increase in global orders for merchandise since April of that year. Future orders of shoes or clothes for delivery between December and April, rose to $10.4 billion.  Nike shares (NKE) rose 0.6 percent to $78.75 in extended trading.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2015, Nike announced it would initiate a $12 billion share buyback, as well as a two-for-one stock split, with shares to begin trading at the decreased price on December 24.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> The split will be the seventh in company history.
</p><p>In June 2018, Nike announced it would initiate a $15 billion share buyback over four years, to begin in 2019 upon completion of the previous buyback program.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup></p><p>For the fiscal year 2018, Nike reported earnings of US$1.933 billion, with an annual revenue of US$36.397 billion, an increase of 6.0% over the previous fiscal cycle. Nike's shares traded at over $72 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over US$114.5 billion in October 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2020, Nike reported a 5% drop in Chinese sales associated with stores' closure due to the COVID-19 outbreak. It was the first decrease in six years. At the same time, the company's online sales grew by 36% during Q1 of 2020. Also, the sales of personal training apps grew by 80% in China.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup></p>
